et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and take a larger splint of linen and bind it above the skin that is over the bone.
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	And stretch out the head, so that you pull out the corrupt flesh below.
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	And uncover the flesh at the joint where you see it should be, so that the skin does not prick the flesh.
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	Put a splint or a board under the bone to cover the corrupt flesh and move it.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	It should be as much as you can see and feel the corruption, and be careful to do it again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	Cover the entire flesh with a hot iron; then place one hot iron on top of it,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and if the corruption is spread from one part to another, and the iron is longer than the length of the corruption as we have said,
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	And if the corruption is at the joint, strike the corrupt joint and break the bone on the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And if the corruption is in the continuity of two joints, there is no remedy but to crush it;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	And if the corruption is at the knuckle of the hand or foot, that is a very difficult matter;
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	However, you must investigate this corruption, how it opened up;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	And clean it in all ways as you can, but let the vein or nerve not oppose you.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	And know that the cutting instrument and the saws for covering these bones are many, according to the position of the bone and the appearance of it.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	And their hardness and subtlety, their thickness and thinness, their largeness and smallness, and their roughness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	And for each similar work, one must prepare their instrument accordingly.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	Know that the operation will show you the tool that you will need, according to the knowledge of this craft.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the methods of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you think about the tool that you need according to what is required.
dou feu	Hot iron (or cautery)
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head of the shoulder may dislocate from within or from outside.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have attempted to treat this with the corrosive medicine (cautery), but it does not help at all,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	if it is necessary to cover that limb until the level of the cautery has healed,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	If the patient is scorched by this [cautery], it may cause death or greater harm to the member due to its fault.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the limb turns black, as if it were burned by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and after the blackness, it goes to the corruption of member by member,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	And takes hold of the whole body; if you hasten to cover it.
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is by the bite of some poisonous animals like sea scorpions, weasels and similar creatures,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If the corruption is at the head of the toe, strike it, and give it no opportunity to come up as far as the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up as far as the hand, strike at the joint, so that the corruption does not come up to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	And if it comes to the arm, strike at the bone; and if it passes the bone, it is death,
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and no remedy foreign works except for the quantity of its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and thus do as when corruption comes or putrefaction: if it comes at the first joint, strike after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to putrefaction, strike the whole area of putrefaction;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	And if it rises in the leg, strike at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	And if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy for the sick man but to kill him;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	The method of healing or treating a limb is that you bind it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	And stretch one minister (bandage) downwards, and another minister (bandage) upwards,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	And you desire the cartilage that is between the two joints at one space of about half an inch wide, until the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then take a copper or silk, and place one linen cloth on each side, so that the silk does not touch the healthy area;
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and bring other wounds and abscesses closed for the patient;
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And when bleeding occurs during your work, cauterize the area immediately.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	and place some powders that restrain [the flow of blood]; then return to your medicine until it is completed.
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the limb with a sturdy rope and heal it until it is healthy.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to one man in a dream:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	It came upon him a blackness that seemed burnt by fire
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and this corrosion first appeared in his tooth root, consuming the entire tooth;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corrosion, he gnawed at the tooth, and it became healthy;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long afterwards the corrosion returned to his hand, and it came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	And I place it on reflective things after the purification of the body, and the corrosion cannot cease.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	It also requires that I cut off the hand, and I do not wish to, unless I have hope of reflecting the matter.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	Also doubted whether if I cut off his hand, he would not die,
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	The strength of man was weak; he lost hope and returned to his land.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and struck himself with a sword in the hand, and was healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And I have never heard of this story except as something that others do when it is needed.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	An abscess may occur in a charnut (charcoal or coals) and remain for so long that it creates a large swelling.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	And then they run and pierce, leap through (it), and hold still the place, just like a squire.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	The skin that is on top is as thin as a linen cloth cut open.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	They will not go to the bone or to the nerve, and such an illness is called "sain."
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	And it is not called "fistula."
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	But if it is so long that it reaches the bone entirely, it is called "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and you should cook that skin all around, and likewise when it is thin, as a bandage.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and not by its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have reason to believe that the skin is rotting, but the rot is not complete,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And the skin is thick with fat, if you cure it with a clistere like this:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	look to see if the breasts are large and the boil that is in them smells bad,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then clisterize with Egyptian medicine made like this:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take asafetida, oil, and litharge, equally, and cook in one pot on fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	While the medicine is red and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	then take from this according to your need, and make it into vinegar and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and anoint the breast and constrict the wound;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	And let the medicine sit for two hours, then remove it by pulling.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Do this often, until the breast is unblocked and the pus is removed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	And sometimes it is cleansed with ashes water,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	When this medicine is absent, and it is that you take vine ash [powder], and pour water over it.
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	Then cook [heat] it and apply as a poultice, until you know that the breast is well healed;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot tolerate it, or Egyptian medicine or water of ashes are not available.
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the poultice contains a little lupine flour, ground.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you bind it with honey and sweetened wine, that the honey has properties of purifying and washing,
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the blood thin;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you have confidence that the breasts are well purified,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if the poultice that causes the pus to form in it,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	And you shall take a plaster made definite, and make it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	and you shall anoint it with certain medicines and unguents, whose properties I have said or treating the unguents;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	if the wound of the breast is small, and the plaster cannot enter,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	if the size of an iron is about a thumb, and you put inside it the Egyptian unguent in a tent;
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	And the ointment of basilicon, when it is diluted.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too wide, then cut [the edges] so that there remains only one league or the plaster can enter.
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the ulcerated boil is above, strike it or lower its level.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	When the bow is fully drawn, do not let it release its string;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the chest underneath as you see;
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	adjust in such a way that the bow aims to the lowest point possible.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	When the bow is fully drawn, do not let it release its string;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	And if you cannot cover the breast under as you see,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	and the bow is to be arranged in this manner: that the bowstring slides easily downwards, and not leave anything of the bow.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidating medicines to put on the breast,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and lay a linen cloth over it that covers the entire breast;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	Then apply force to the wound of the chest. That is, a little larger than the first one,
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	Next, apply anointing oil or other cloth according to the size of the wound,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and place it over the wound on the chest to align the bone, but do not remove the large cloth until after many days once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	And he who is on the breastbone, often broken to remove the breastbone,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and know what happens when the breastbone is cut, whether it's poisoned or injured, or digestible, or undigested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has been spread in this manner, and you see the bone protruding from the breastbone,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	If you know that breasts shrink (or atrophy), approach them.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then undress him in the morning or the third hour, and when you undress the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	change one other bandage and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast becomes swollen indigest after many days, know that breasts do not shrink (atrophy).
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle poisons court after a long time, do not despair of health.
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	for the healing approaches. For there are men whose wounds delay in healing and those who act against it.
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	if the stomach swells undigested after many days, know that the breast does not heal easily.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	if the breast delays in swelling and is protruding, apply dry yet moist medicines in substance and dry in virtue.
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	As with an eggshell, because it contains much glass, which is its last remedy.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take the eggshell as defined, and make it with rose oil, and stir equal parts of old wine in substance;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook and use it; and similarly, this done more cooked and swollen,
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when eggshells defined are not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	Take myrrh and aloe and incense, grind them together, then sprinkle the powder on honey when it is over the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then place one cloth on it and set it over the breast, and sometimes an astrologer is administered long oil;
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and the roots of celestial lilies, which are like flour and coriander.
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and use simple or compound remedies: grind them, make powder, and put it on the honey I mentioned, and use.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	And if the wound is long and not treated by this treatment,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that corruption has entered completely, and causes pressure on the bone or hard parts, or the ligaments;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the treatment for fistula is applied, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the abscess of the nailbed
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Pancreatis is an abscess that arises under the nail of the finger.
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	and sometimes it arises in other toes;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is neglected and no care is taken, one abscess follows another.
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and they will run and empty the boil until it reaches the root of the nail, and by chance, they may burst it completely.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	And comes the corruption up to the bone, until it brings foul pain, and the head is wide, and the color turns red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, but the treatment does not help at all.
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	If it doesn't help, then you must cut into it. Remove all the superfluidity that remains from the nail.
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	Then cauterize the wound after.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauteries are very great aid if the bone is healthy, and the nail is intact;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail penetrates the flesh afterward and begins to swell and bruise,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	You must place the salve under the nail so as not to touch the flesh;
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	And push upward, and strike the flesh gently and lightly.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	And place on top of the remaining flesh the remnant of the hot and corrosive medical charcoal to burn everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, heal him with ointments until he is healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, strike it and draw it, for as much as the bone is corrupted there, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the tooth corrupted, strike it in one of the nails as stated before,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal it until it is healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is wounded, pierced, and causes great pain, you must first heal the wound.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	Then cut the spur with a sharp spatula from above, crossing it.
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and be careful that the cutting does not reach the flesh beneath the spur, for the patient would feel too great pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	if it happens, place something on top to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The patient must adjust the one who is born in the hand of some men by chance, which is entirely fleshy.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and by chance it has bone or nail, and sometimes it has a claw.
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and one of these is born in the root of the joint, or its growth is in some of our fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	The one that is born in any knuckle of the finger does not move.
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	And the one born at the joint of the thumb, by chance may remain silent;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the length of the one who is fat is light, in this way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	the length from its root to a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	The one born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure: hold it with a cover;
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In one who is born or will soon die, it is necessary that you cut open the round flesh up to the bone.
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cut the bone with an appropriate saw, then heal it until it heals.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The same sores that come to the joints come together due to birth, or due to injury from a wound, or by burning with fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary that you cut the sores in such a way that they heal according to their natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then place between two tents or dampened cloths soaked in rose oil, so that they do not stick;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you place between two thin boards until the wound is sutured, as necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	Also, if any of its two sides comes with the palm, strike that suture as needed.
Des vils	Of simple men
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The veins are large, swollen, filled with melancholic fluids that come in many members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And it happens more in the legs of those who walk and work and carry, rather than others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must administer purges of gall and then cleanse the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment of iron is in two ways: one way is to strike it, and blood black fluid will be drawn out.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And another way is to open a vein and pull it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The procedure is as follows: make an incision in the leg with strong hot water, until the flesh becomes tender.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	Then restrain the leg of the patient from above the knee to the part below the thigh;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	Then open the vein in one, two or three places, of a large size,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then slice and draw out the black blood from your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood flows out as the sickness can tolerate.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	And then tie it and command that he bind himself with foods strengthening black bile.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and repeat the evacuation and healing when the veins are full, and this benefits the sick person.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The swellings of it (the affected part) are to be handled in this manner: raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then immerse it (the affected part) in water and apply warm, moist compresses to the swelling until it turns red and swells up.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	if you don't have any water, heat it (the affected part) over the fire and then apply long compresses to the swelling at the knee or in the area below the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then grind the hide into paste and scrape off the swelling from both sides until it appears when you feel it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	And one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin, it appears as a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	Then push the rod underneath, while it is raised on the skin, and then break it at the slight bend.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	Then strike in another place three finger-widths away; then flay the skin above the vein as far as it appears.
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then tie the cord as you have done, and break it at another bend, as you did before.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then cut another size, or more if needed, then heat it, and apply it to the base of the foot.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then draw and heat it up to the second size; then cut it from size to size, until it becomes hot all the way through, then apply it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot draw and heat it, put a thick, double-threaded needle into it.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	pull it and heat it, and put a rope underneath, and turn your hand from one side to the other until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And keep it from healing over, for if it heals over, it cannot be drawn or lifted, and harm comes to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have treated it all, lay on the wound linen wet with vinegar and oil of roses; and let it heal until it is sound.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	If the eyes are constricted, twisted, and swollen together and they are not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	If it is necessary to cut it forcefully, but do not cover it; draw it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of iron used to pierce the vein is curved and does not cut, it should not pierce the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of large curvature, because if it is subtle, it would pierce the vein, but be thick as we have said, and here is its shape:
De la voinne civile	From the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is incised in the legs, in warm parts where no grass or trees grow, and on land with no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	And by chance it arises elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to corruption that comes beneath the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	As a serpent within the body twists and turns, cut between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that there is a very large inflammation in the leg,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	Then the limb changes, and the vein begins to emerge, as the root of a plant does.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the shoulder opens up, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of wood from 6 to 12 inches long and tie it.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the wood on the leg, and every time it moves away from its place, you wrap around the wood again and tie it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut a part of it and wrap the rest, but do not cover its root until it has all come out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cut it, it will return into the flesh, causing an abscess or pus and a bad disease.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	For that thing it is necessary that it be treated little by little up to the head, and not remain anything in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	And sometimes this vein, when it is treated from 5 to 10 fingers long,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and one man came to me, from whom it issued from 10 fingers long, and when you cut it, if you press it with a knife or lancet, and pierce it until bottom,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that everything goes out; and empty the matter that is inside, and bring medicine for it to the place, in the form of a plaster or poultice within a day, then cure it like an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes at this vein, many hands are placed, and especially when it opens in the joint of the foot or ankle,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and much blood flows out, and it jumps around; heal it then as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called "cattle disease" in our land because it often occurs in cattle,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	And it is a small worm that grows between skin and flesh, which travels throughout the body swelling and shrinking.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	It causes pain in one member after another as it moves under the skin where it goes, and it jumps out of place.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	It is caused by corruption of certain humors such as worms, snakes, lice, and roundworms or stomach parasites.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	One doubts its malignancy as when it travels through the body, it moves towards the head and reaches the eyes.
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	By chance, it enters (the body) and destroys oil; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see him to cure and draw, one can force it only when he goes (moves):
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	Then it is necessary that you tie the limb above and below with a strong cord tightly:
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then strike above (the wound) and draw out forcefully, and if the blood flows in full into the flesh, you do not pull it:
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	If you apply fire cautery until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greater damage it causes, that is when it burns oil, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it approaching or close to the oil, hold a cork beneath it in shape, then strike above, and pull it out.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is necessary for the patient to use body cleansing with dissolving medicines to remove bad humors.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And it swells with meat pork putrefaction.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called "vakirir" on our land, and is a pain that comes in some limbs,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and moves from one limb to another; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was summoned to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and saw a small swelling in the armpit of the arm.
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and later, it appeared to rise like a worm towards the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	more quickly than anything else, like living silver when it is cut from one piece.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain separated from that place and pierced into the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	And shortly after, it ran through the entire body, until it came to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then I found that it was turning around the body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how it moved from member to member, because I had never seen this disease in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had often seen pain move from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I did not want it at all, as I saw it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins exposed.
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and for this reason, such constrained wind appears;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it does not apply to those who are voluptuous and have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	then press above and below firmly, and then press downwards until the windiness is confined to its place.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	cauterize the area; and if you do not see it in your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if you cure the one who suffers from windiness, as with foul-smelling pills and pills of snake-root, and similar things.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are of various kinds, according to their shapes and the places in the body where they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity is that there are those with large points, and small, curved, and hafted.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those that have two points, and of those that have tongues, and of those where there are splinters.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and dislocation occurs in any member falls in two ways: either in a principal member,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in a secondary member, such as the brain, heart, liver, spleen, lungs, intestines, bladder and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When dislocation occurs in any of these members, the signs of death which I will tell you later will reveal themselves:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	If you are dealing with the extraction of this arrow, you should be aware that death can come in many positions;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when this bad sign does not appear and the arrow is not fully out, pull it and heal the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And when the head of the skull is struck by the arrow and pierces the bone, the person who is on top of the head should push it outward.
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	This is for the removal of a cataract and suturing, eye drops and redness reduction, throat inflammation and redness, spasm and confusion of thought, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	And by chance it happens without force from the nostrils, or from the ears; and by chance, it loses speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	And leaps out of the wound white moisture resembling pus, and leaps likewise like bubbles of boiling oil.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if this sign appears, refrain from treatment, and draw the arrow if it is not in (the wound).
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it falls or pierces through is that it is near the left breast and feels like it has been inserted into something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And sometimes the patient becomes silent like a corpse, and there is black blood in the urine, and coldness and cold sweat, and faintness.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Then it is clear that death is at hand.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The sign of an arrow that has not penetrated the flesh is when there is no scum coming from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, breathes heavily and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	If the arrow falls on the bed cover, it has missed the ribs; and it causes great pain and sighing, and all the limbs of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrowhead or stomach falls out of the wound by chance, any undigested meat may jump from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrowhead or stomach falls out by chance and anything from the intestines escapes through the wound, there is no hope for recovery nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrowhead falls into the bladder and urine escapes and leaks out, causing the patient great pain: know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, such as the arm and neck, shoulder and joints of the shoulder, spine of the back, rib cage and thighs, legs, and limbs resembling them, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it's not poisoned, as I will tell you what happened to me, you should do this:
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	There was a man who had an arrow lodged or embedded in the root of his neck:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I pulled it out from another side below the ear fat, and it came out without any damage to the senses.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And draw out an arrow which falls in the oil fat below the paper beneath,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was reversed, and could not be reached except by the tip towards the flesh,
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was large like a Turkish bow, all of one piece with no feathers; the game was safe, and no adverse incident happened.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And remove an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I was the beards (barbions), and softened it as much as I could before removing it, and the Christian recovered.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And removed an arrow from a man who was either head or belly (cheued or ventred), and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after he had passed thirty days, his condition did not improve;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrowhead, and bent it, and drew it out without any adverse consequences.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you want to treat a man who has an arrow lodged or stuck in his flesh, and the wound is healed over it;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remained inside him, and did not destroy his natural positioning,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	It finds no harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And it is for another man who has an arrow lodged in his flesh and the wound has healed over.
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And he endured thus without suffering great pain, and many similar things.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And it drew an arrow from one of the prince's men, who had fallen in enemy territory,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	And it was slightly inclined to the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was summoned for treatment after she fell for three days. I found the wound narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I drew it out with a very fine wire, but felt no sensation.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	And he felt sharp pain and discomfort beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I think this is of the point of the arrowhead
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I place the plaster on the ulcerative, absorptive, and digestive area, because they do not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and appeared the arrow wound.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I applied the plaster for several days, and healed the wound directly, and kept the patient for a long time,
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	As long as he feels the arrow within his body for a day, he tells it to you.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I apply medicinal ointment containing corrosive agents on the wound for several days until it is healed.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I probe it, and feel the head of the arrow that protrudes from its place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then I placed the arrowhead in the wound opening with that corrosive ointment until the head of the arrow became visible.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	And he passed beyond the limits within 4 months.
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	Then open the wound that I pierced with the tweezers, and stretch it from one side to another, and it could not come out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Then I did not stop experimenting and inventing methods with various instruments until I had made the tweezers well after 1 hour.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	According to what his form comes at the end of this chapter, as long as I stay and return the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the physicians judge that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	Then I will restore it, and the wound will heal, and the patient will be entirely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	And I have told you the quality of arrow extraction,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you apply your knowledge to this matter, for books cannot cover everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	But surgeons, skilled in little, compare well with what is present and failing.
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	They understand nine works and nine tools for the treatment of foreign things happening in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not enter the limbs they are inserted into except by two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either through the side or from another direction.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and the one which jumps out through the hole where it enters, is an arrow entering flesh, and jumps out sometimes now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump out, let it be until the flesh is opened around, and the wound closed;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And in the same way, if it is fixed in the bone and cannot be pulled out, leave it for several days, and turn it every day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it jumps, and if it does not jump, pierce all around with a sharp instrument, until the surrounding areas are enlarged, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	If the arrow is driven into the bone of the head, and goes to one of the cavities of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	And some of the accidents that I have said to the patient: do not draw it out at all, but let it be equal after several days.
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the arrow reaches its mark, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is only lodged in the bone but does not reach its mark,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	The patient may live for some days without serious complication if the wound is properly treated.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is deeply lodged and cannot be extracted, administer tourniquets as I have told you, then treat the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is returned to its place within the body which cannot be seen, pull it with all your strength.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, draw it out with any suitable instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if due to the narrowness of the wound or the deep penetration of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if there is no bone, tendon, or vein, make an incision large enough for the wound to be wide open.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	And pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears like it clings to something in the arrow.
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	and drill a hole through the bone that is pierced by two parts, as far as you can.
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the arrow, until you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	be careful not to break the arrow when trying to remove it.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, then lay the body down towards its joints, then pull, because the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the bleeding causes problems, bring to mind what we have said about its treatment in this chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of cutting the nerve and vein, and use devices as you can pull out the arrow safely,
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; place the patient according to the shape he was in when the arrow struck him,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	For it is the greatest aid that there can be, and if you cannot do it, follow what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	Arrows that come from another place, or it opens something of them, or the skin is swollen in that area as we can see or feel it.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Make an incision there, as long as the pincers can grasp it, and then pull it out if it is still there.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	If the arrowhead is lodged in the bone, turn your hand round, so it enters into the bone and expand the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then continue the extraction until it comes forth;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if it be of the arrowhead, push it all the way through;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	if it be fallen and you wish to administer a potion, administer one hair-length of the potion.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	The point of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument; then push forcefully.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is embedded, apply the instrument point entering in, to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is touched, then you must cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if possible.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	Then heal the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if an arrow falls or pierces the belly or bladder or side, and it is close by and you can cover it, then cover it.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And be careful to not cover the vein and nerve, then pull it out, and then sew up the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and let it heal completely.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pliers used to extract arrows is similar to an owl's beak, as shown here:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways of doing it: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrowhead.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape at the end of the hair is also like the feather of a bird.
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to point the arrowhead, as in this shape here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pliers for pushing and pulling is as follows here:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Of the common veins (of the body)
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	The number of veins one drains is thirty-one, and from that one takes off sixteen as head (or principal ones).
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	That is to say: two veins located behind the ears, called the "double herb" (or double venae comitantes);
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries in each temple that are visible;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And two veins which are in each of the two eyes, called "aspirates".
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	And the vein that is on the forehead; and the vein that is at the head of the nose.
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	And the two glands that are in the neck.
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	And the two veins that are above the lips on the mouth, and these veins are called "augeherich".
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	These are the veins located beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins that are commonly known to be five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	The one is called the cephalic, and it is on the left side of the chest, and the common people call it "vein of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	And the middle [part] is called "fast", consisting of the cephalic and basilic.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And laymen call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	And laymen call it "vein of the abdomen", and it is above the liver,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And this is the one that is healed, which opens clearly over the pocket.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	The salve is the vein which is between the ring finger and little finger, and has two ribs;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	And in the leg and foot there are four veins: one is beneath the hollow of the pocket on the left side,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	And the second saphenous vein, which is at the wrist on the right side; and the vein called "nase", which is in the wrist of the left side;
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other leg there are three veins beneath them.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The vein after the ears helps with old catarrhs and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the qualities of the vein, as I tell you, and it is that you raise the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	And rub the joint or veins with a rough cloth; then hold the patient's neck with a screw.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending on the head.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	then press there, and where you feel the pulse below your neck, press firmly.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lance, and thrust it through the vein to the bone, then withdraw your hand from the entire vein upward.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	And pierce the skin and the vein well with two incisions of thumb breadth, and let the blood issue as much as you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then strain and tie it, until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The healing of the two arteries that are in the two temples, is worth migraines in the old way,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	And [the patient should] soothe, and treat eye ailments, and dry the tears of eyes that itch.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the qualities of the healer are as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is necessary for the patient to stretch out their neck so that the two veins appear openly.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	And the foot is swollen under your throat, then squeeze it.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	Then lift the cure on top of the vein at your thumb, and thrust the lancet beneath it.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	lift the vein upwards, then cut it, just as you have done in two other veins, and make a hole for the blood according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then release the patient, place your thumb on the vein for an hour, then place cotton over it.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And then form the ligature and leave it until it heals; and we have spoken about its dressing and extraction, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing of the vein in the forehead is worth as much as the healing of the skull for the ancient diseases of the face, and it has migrated, turned red.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And the quality is that the patient stretches his neck in twisting, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument called "fosseur", which is shaped as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip on the vein, hold above your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then cut the neck of the patient and tie the vein until it is healthy and not open at any time with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, the flames should not be too sharp; and the vein should be pierced transversely, as the bone is near, and in case the flames are too thin, they might break when they are too fine.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The salve of the two veins that are in the armpits helps the eyes, and the tinge, and the swelling, and the ulcer in the oil, and the diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the qualities of their salve are such that the patient stretches his neck by twisting with some chain, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then the salve, and the salve of the iron rod, a little bit long, a little bit wide, because it has no heat.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, they may break; then make the wound bleed, as much as needed, and then cover it with linen, and hold it in place.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The vein from the neck is useful for ague (intermittent fever), scurvy, and facial diseases.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	as well as headache and redness that comes in the face, especially when it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	And the qualities of the blood are such that the patient squeezes their neck, then squeezes their nose with your left hand.
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take the subtle flame long, and thrust it in through the opening between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	because the veins do not open easily, and the wounds will not start to heal now.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	do not go too deep, and make the wound bleed according to your need, then let it heal for a night, because it is very quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	And this is the shape of fire:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The salve of two gums helps in the stretching of the anus, and at the beginning of inflammation, and in many diseases, and in stopping itching, and in corroding, and in sores, and in abscesses;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the qualities of the salve are that the patient pulls out his neck from under one and the other, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	And let the master stand over the head of the patient, and the patient sit on one seat.
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	Then open the vein longwise a little widely, then draw out the blood moderately, as much as necessary;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	Then do the same on the other side, then release the ligament, and tie both veins moderately,
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and let it be until the morning, so that the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	Of the liver purge
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	For the purging of the veins in the lips above, it helps for coughing in the mouth, and for the corruption of the gums, and for cracks in the lips, and for the toothache and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the purging is to make the patient sit before you, and to hold his neck as I said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	Then turn the lip and look at the two veins, one on the right side of the upper lip and the other on the left side,
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	And they are recognized by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	Then press them gently, and if you do not recognize them, and you doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	press the larger of each pair, and likewise do the two veins above and below, for it is the same way.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	The purging under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The soreness of veins located under the tongue helps after the head injury, and it is at the constriction of the throat, and with diseases of the eye, and with diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the qualities of soothing are that the patient should be seated between his hands facing the sun, and he lifts the tongue, and looks under each side at a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	therefore, both should be done, but do not go too deep, for below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the cost, which are commonly healed, are healed according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	Or when pricking with all sorts of fire, either coarse myrtle or subtle olive oil as you cut through, and it is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and thin according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirtin is very famous, and is wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it must be necessary to open the veins with thick blood appearing, and those containing thick blood and disorder.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of olive oil flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more pointed and subtle, for cleansing thin veins with subtle blood or yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these vessels, helps with diseases that are below the throat, neck and abdomen.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is necessary for the patient to bleed profusely, and to empty the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if it touches the artery, and bleeding occurs, it should be stopped, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And the flame should not be pointed at, but cut with a knife instead.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open clearly, you must force it open and replace another one.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you want no pain from it, or you heal in its place the vein by cutting into the arm: it opens clearly.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and apply the copper cup to the fire as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to find the vein's place, then you must first stretch out the arm and touch it until you feel the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then mark the place with a cross, then bind the arm, and burn the vein with the flame cauter.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And be careful not to cut into the artery when you see the place swell, because that is the artery; then avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	If you see it swell up high like the urine of a child, and if it is red and thin, know that it is not an artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry up then, and place your hand on it for a long time, then remove your hand from it without stopping, as this happens repeatedly;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	Bind the arm and let it be in that position, do not move it by the patient; and be afraid and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the wound does not stop bleeding and the medicine is not present, stop the artery if it is open, for the head of the limb will retract; stop the bleeding from the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	Take a strip of the plaster-of-Paris, cut it and take one half and bind it above the other for a day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If it (the wound) does not stop bleeding, that's good; if it doesn't, treat it as we have said, with powders that stop blood flow.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the application (of the powder) should not be too strong in many positions due to the small size of the wound and the weakness of the ligament in the arm.
