Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The vein wounding in the middle helps to treat blood in the head above and in the body below,
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilica and the cephalic, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	And it is necessary for the lord [physician] to probe with a finger for the nerve that is underneath, and if it pricks too deep, and he touches the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells and the patient feels pain, and perhaps it cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens frequently, and if it does not open in any man due to his subtlety, you must cauterize it with the instrument; and cut off the nerve with your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The sanitation of the skull helps, since it draws blood from the head, assists the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	It is necessary to sanitize when pricking with olive oil or myrtle fire, for it is the safest of all veins, since there is neither nerve nor artery underneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Furthermore, it is necessary to seek out the easier joint, and not to be distressed if it needs to be done the first time, and then we repeat.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And by chance, the joints swell in some men, when it needs to be done the first time, but do not be distressed.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the wound, according to your judgment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about dressing a wound is that it is brought only for the sake of preserving health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to prevent future illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	And let the incision be made in one of the three veins that are called: cephalic, femoral, and basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And it should be incised at the beginning of spring, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of fullness appear.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	And it should be incised on the first or third day, after two or four hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The incision administered for diseases does not have a specific time duration, but when it is needed at day or night, in all hours and at any time;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	It is not advisable to cleanse children until they are 14 years old, nor should a woman carry fire except during the fourth month up to the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	It is not necessary to cleanse those who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when anyone wishes to be cleansed, in whatever way that may be, it is necessary that they purge the intestines with a light enema.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if there is much bad air retained, so that the veins do not carry away the superfluous waste from the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	He who is excessively salted with foods, drunk, or watery-dropped, cannot heal.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if he is washed to heal after colic affliction, vomiting, diarrhea of the belly, multiplying of abstinence from women, labor, watching, and praying, and those who exhaust their strength or by something of the weapon or the body.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then refine the humors, if he is fat, with foods and drinks and medications, if you have the power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	Then immerse where bath, if nothing prevents it, to refine the blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and clean the vein with the tip of the third finger, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep that day from work, from pain, and from lust, and similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and bind and cleanse, and let the bandages be higher than those who are being cleansed, and wipe the arm twice or thrice.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then gently pull the ligament above, for if it is too tight or weak, it cannot be corrected without.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the joint with hands until the veins swell and feel them.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	Then wet the bandages with a little bit of old oil, then put your thumb of your left hand on that vein under the joint where you want to bind it.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not break when cutting.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that run like cords on a sieve, and some of them are filled with windiness,
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	when fire is applied, it pulls back from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of those.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if it opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, which means the sieve must be careful in such matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens for the first time, that is good; but if not, continue again under that place or near immediately, unless the wound is inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the joint is swollen, and the patient fears, he should rest for one day or two, and never tie the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	Perhaps it will come abscesses covered with cloths; do not enter or bathe, then resume the healing if he wishes.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the opening is small or without court (cort), carefully probe it and you doubt that blood flows as much as you see, trust in the opening itself directly with all flame.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and open it slightly hastily, so that the joint is not swollen; for this happens often when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the joint swollen, do not start the bleeding, and put some oil of lilies on it, for it will cool the body's blood and make the liquid in this joint similar to oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and in the same manner administer the oil of lilies during each bleeding process, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and this same substance is filtered through a strainer and boiled when it is put onto the joint; if it becomes too thick, filter it until it becomes thin.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes a large abscess, which often happens, especially when the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	then press it with a damp sponge in vinegar and hot oil for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and you must do this after the blood has left the vein, and if it remains in place after some days without any black or greenness, that is not harmful;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see it, put something of aloe or myrrh preserved in oil of roses, camphor, or similar things on top of it.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often abscess and appearance occur at the opening of the basilica: place your hand on it then, if you find the area soft under the pressure of your hand, this is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	But do not apply any of the things we have said, because possibly it is an artery; but place one dry bandage to stiffen it, then treat with another cure until it heals.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	Draw blood from each (wound) according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	If the wound is black, let it drain until it turns red; if you see it swollen, let it drain until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for those who are cut and open, and need bloodletting, make the incision wider, and let the veins be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for those who are weak, do the opposite, and it must be bled little by little, and it should be bled by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of incision is safe from the disorder of bleeding and damage to nerves, and it should be done in length rather than width.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	To the body that needs to be incised, it is necessary to give soft bread below grape-like pomegranates; if it is scalded, let it bleed four or five times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if it is of cold constitution, eat soft bread moistened in sweet syrup or honey-scented syrup with spices like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and sugar, and fragrant syrup before the incision.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if it swells at the wound, after the evacuation of much blood, it is required that you apply a poultice of charcoal and a fragrant subtle syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use other things as we have said in the section or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	If you want to burst open the arm or heal it again at another time, when it is weakened by much bloodletting, it is required that it be bled little by little according to its continuous strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	If you want to burst open the arm after the first bloodletting and one has a strong chest, it should be bled 6 hours after the first bloodletting or the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to heal from another part, must heal by the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For there is much blood within the body which is already overheated, and causes fever; therefore a large quantity must be drawn out, and the opening widened until it breaks.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	Then, when you have treated all the conditions of healing, place your hand on top of the wound so that death does not come to the opening.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	And this often happens when surgeons are negligent.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	Do not remove the arm from its sling, make an incision again and let the wound bleed a second time, and if the flesh is closed, you must press firmly.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If it's curved, do not stretch the arm forcefully, as it would be harmful.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	But leave it until it heals the second time. Or you can apply heat to the wound with a pointed flame, until the frozen blood comes out from the vein.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	And place on it (the wound) about one piece of wool soaked in vinegar, and press gently on top.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	If the vein is burst, leave it be and do not squeeze it until the abscess has been calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	If there is a need to draw blood again, then take it from the same place, or another vein, or the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm are composed of many small veins.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of the sanity is that the patient dips his hand in hot water until the flesh becomes red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then tie it moderately, so that the vein appears clearly, and then pierce with a crosswise stroke, neither too wide nor too long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and make the holes large, and pierce the vein close to the wrist joint, and if it does not bleed, put the hand back in hot water, and let the blood run into the water until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is summer, do not immerse the hand in hot water again, because it is colder in summer than in winter.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the vein of this vessel is safer than all other vessels, as there are neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The vein of the left arm is worth for all liver diseases, and this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Hold the hand and push into hot water until the vein is emptied, if you can see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if the vein is crossed over, and you cut it completely through all, it causes no harm.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	Do not go too deep because nerves are underneath all bare.
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Then put the hand in hot water, if the wound is not frozen, and it cannot be drained out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drained the blood as needed, place oil and wax on top of the vein to seal it quickly, and do the same for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The poultice on the left hand is good for the disease of the mouse, and do as I told you with the right one.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The poultice made from soap is good for all diseases that are below the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	and for diseases of the uterus, and retention of menses, and diseases of the kidneys and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the qualities of his health are such that the patient should put his foot in hot water and rub over the vein until it perishes.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and on the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and from below the foot there are many rain-like things.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Therefore take the larger rain, or at the ankle, which is more useful.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	If you cleanse above the foot, guard against the nerves that are below, and cleanse through it as well, in the same way as when cutting; and let the fire be extinguished.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the limb cannot come out, put it into water and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	If the lancing is necessary for the first time, then repeat it slightly above, because the wound is salted;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not be afraid of the nerve, as we have said, and similarly treat the other limb equally with soap.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The thigh of the sciatic nerve is at the knee joint, and its pain resembles that of the hamstring when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the qualities of its pain are such that the patient immerses themselves in water and squeezes above the knee joint four fingers twisting it.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	because otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, you should drain it in all possible ways and across.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it moves that you cut it, because the thigh is hollow, and it is very responsive to human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you don't pull it out, no cure will open or close the small of the foot, and beware of nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	then let the blood coagulate as you see fit, and then untie the ligature, place cotton on it and compress; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Blisters of the bladder
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses are made of horns, or of iron, or of glass; and ventosing is done in two ways: either by wounding and drawing blood, or without wounding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this ventosing which is done without wounding, is in two ways: either it is at all fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	And ventosing which is done by wounding and extraction of blood, is done in 14 places on the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	Of this, one is completely asleep (or unconscious); and the others are (be) choked by the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two more on each side of the neck; and the wounds under the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and wounds on both shoulders; and wounds on the knees;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and wounds on both arms; and wounds on both legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	And the boils of the two shins; and the boils do not bleed, unless from small veins scattered in the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and because of this, you should not drain them at all, as one does with bleeding from a vein.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be administered, neither with fire nor hot water, in any disease that comes from swelling, until the entire body is purged.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	If it is necessary for the treatment of diseases to bleed, or according to custom, we will administer it every hour at the beginning or end of the month, or in between, and at any other time.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are some who, when they need to vomit, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and those who find themselves with fullness and redness in their body, and in their head, and at the neck, and blindness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, with swollen tongue, and ooze blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are some who are delirious, see things through blurry blood, have nosebleeds, vomiting, and similar things;
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially if it is at the end of the month, we order to bleed them after 3 hours from dawn.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The purgation of the bladder helps alleviate headaches ... that come to the eyes, and it is not advisable that this be done after the evacuation of the entire body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this bleeding is in place of bladder purgation,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And it is not suitable for one of cold constitution to use [this treatment], or who has scurvy, for it does them great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	For this reason, the elderly should not use it, nor those with cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who heal themselves often become negligent, and for this reason, the bellows should be placed a little lower due to the fear of neglect.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The bellows at the neck is in the position for healing the head and the basilica, and therefore it is beneficial for treating fractures.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and to cut open the channel of the femur, and in all, and in fullness;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	it should be pushed gently, for if it holds too tightly, it may cause obstruction or intestinal or heart problems.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	Windbladder in the two ribs of the neck is worth the headache, and otalgia and migraine, and strangulation, and pain in the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it is in the place of the basilica's saint; you must instruct the lord to extend his hand to place it, not to touch the artery, and no bleeding should occur.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Ventilations under the chin are beneficial for mouth diseases, tooth decay, and similar mouth illnesses; they are located at the saint sites of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilations on the shoulders are beneficial for illness resulting from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The ventosations of the sides are worth as much as three veins from the arm.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	for it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and commands the lord not to let him plunge too deep, for the limb is naked of flesh, and knows beneath black and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The ventosation that is on the rump is worth as much as emorroids from the foundation and diseases below, and it must be large, and made of iron, for it needs to draw well; and if it were too thin, it would break, causing large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The swellings of the legs open widely because they draw blood from the entire body; they cause ancient pains of the kidneys, bladder, and urinary tract, and reduce the flowers [in the body]; they are in the places of the knees and ankles, and everywhere else they weaken the body after long use, and bring pus to many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the swelling is that you first empty it, suck immediately and press hastily, move equally, and do not stop doing this until you see the place red and inflated, and open the red color of the blood; then fart, and return the swellings, and take care in the disposition of the body, for there are some who have hard flesh and clear pores: it is necessary to pierce only once, and it is necessary to make wide wounds, and a little deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the flesh is thick, it is necessary to pierce twice: the first time to refine the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the bone is very thick, it should be struck three times; and when we wish to draw blood drop by drop, we must pierce only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	If we want a large amount of blood, we must repeatedly strike it; and if the bone is thick, we should strike through to its end, and make sure that the veins are pierced suddenly,
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it is necessary for those with thick and hard skin, and narrow pores, to anoint the joints of the shoulders with sharp and dissolving oil:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is oil of violets, olive oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil from seeds of cucumber;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is vinegar, oil of parsley, lilies, chamomile, or similar;
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	and if the superfluidity is thick and cold, take bitter almond oil, or balm oil, or anise oil, and similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	If the person you are treating has thin and narrow pores, no oil should be applied.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	But it is necessary to wash after the dislocation with rose water, or cold water, or water of morello cherries, or water of curcubit, or water of porcelain, or any other similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And one who has much moisture, if he rises from ashes or from myrtle water and sumac and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have great surplus rise from old wine or sour water, or a decoction of fennel or chamomile, or similar.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	And it is not appropriate to use cupping before bathing nor in bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and do not sleep after cupping.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And it is necessary that he urinate, when he should be cupped and after being cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	Watch the one who is bloodletting is coleric, and if he is not, he is too sharp and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	It is necessary that he takes cold things, such as pomegranates and endive and lettuce leaves and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And cooked peas, meat pudding, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold constitution should take honey syrup and moderately aged fragrant wine, and eat cooked peas and cooked beans and small birds and young birds;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day he vomits, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is necessary to give certain men sometimes triticale or muscatel before the fainting, or after, to strengthen the main limbs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And the voids should be plugged, but it is not good that those who are hot drink them.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The voids that are placed near injury are those placed on the liver, spleen, gout, stomach, belly and back, because these members cannot bear injury above them;
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	And it should not be done except to draw blood from one member to another,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	As we do with the testicles when the man suffers from congestion in a member; to remove the thick fluid that is present in the member, as we use leeches on the belly and on the buttocks to reduce the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and relieve the pain when there is obstruction or a stone; it removes the obstruction by its attractive virtue, or expels the stone from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and in this way it is done when it is placed on the liver and the spleen when there is retained wind,
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	And these blisters are treated empty by sucking only; sometimes they are treated with fire, and sometimes filled with cold water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as in diseases of the lungs, and in this way, the blister is filled with hot water or water in which cooked herbs have been infused.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the blister treated with fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it should have two holes of about one and a half palm-widths in length and width, and have one small hole pierced around the navel, just like pushing a needle.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and be made of ivory, soft in front so that it does not prick the patient when placed on the limb.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and have in the middle a bar of ivory or iron, to insert a candle holder.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and they should be large and small according to the diseases and the age of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the umbilical cords of children are different than those of adults, and thin ones from fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should place this umbilical cord over the member in this manner:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	Take a beeswax suppository or linen thread and insert it through the umbilical cord across the rod that is inside the umbilical cord,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	The light should be deep within the bladder so as not to burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	And place it on the member (in this case referring to the affected area), and your fingers should be above the bladder opening as we have said, so that when you look at it, if you see steam coming out, then remove the bladder.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	Take linen as previously described, and repeat this process as needed if required.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the bladder administered in pleurisy, there should be no vein or opening, and it is only to be used when full of fluid. It is placed on the affected area only.
et c’est li forme:	And this is the shape:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Sutures are not brought in except for members where no bladders can be placed due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in bare skin areas like the palm of the hand or soles of the feet, and other similar places;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And the qualities of the user are such that when you find sores in clear, sweet waters without purulent matter, you should take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in clean water, while they are still familiar and have nothing inside of them.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	Then purge it with wine and vinegar, then rub the member until it is red, and place the sores on top.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	And when they are full and hot, if it is possible to apply vinegar, do so, because it is very beneficial.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If it is not so, raise the limb upwards, then downwards gently, and afterwards press it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the limb is not healthy enough after the body, moisten one linen cloth in cold water and place it on top, until the wound is dried.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if the wound is multiplying, put broken glass or salve, and similar things on top until it is dried.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Or place half-peeled beans on the limb and leave them until they harden onto the limb, which will dry it now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you need more, take other snares (or traps)
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	If the snares do not want to catch, then apply fresh blood to the wound and insert a needle until it bleeds.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	Then place them on top, and as soon as they feel the blood, they harden (or congeal).
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they weep, sprinkle a little of aloe powder and crushed sea shell or ash on them, now they will stop weeping.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine and is about the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear child, that the foolish fools of this chapter will never see any old books or read a single letter from them;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason, the science is imported into our land, for I never found any good in it.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing about it except from the knowledge of ancient books, where I have studied the science extensively and treated it by experience, and through the custom of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	I have described in this chapter what is contained within it, and have summarized it at the end, and have made clear the forms of instruments that are brought forth, just as I did in these two chapters beforehand.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore we shall now say the prologue of this book, the sums of the words and the chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and dwell on truth so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fracture or dislocation or twisting or sprain comes to anyone, it is necessary that you straighten the patient from both sides, unless anything prevents you, such as weakness of body, or infants, or elderly people.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	Or if the time is not very hot or too cold; and drink cold broth, that is to say cold broths, and meat of eye and shin, and does not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and does not fill himself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt about abscessing heat or spreading matter in the member; then the patient returns to his first care as he has used it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones start to heal, it is necessary that you nourish the patient with foods that make good nourishment, or he has viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and meat of veal, beef, head, feet, pancreas, fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For by great nursing, the wounds are made worse and break more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of the old and the weak cannot be well healed nor sutured according to their nature due to the lack of strength in the limbs, neither those who are too tender, like those of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but there is no cure for it, bind above the broken bone with large splints that support and join the limb together as before; and do not let it move at all, and for this reason you must feed it with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the neck is other than the break of the foot or of the leg; and I will tell you in this chapter all ways of break.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	There are breaks that heal on their own without setting, and others that need to be set in the manner of cutting the feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is a fracture with an open wound, or a fracture with just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each method shall have its tool, and its appropriate instrument in the restoration, according to what memory comes into its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And it is known that bone fractures occur when the bones are twisted and opened widely by bending, and it should be pressed with the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting or touching, and the patient feels no great pain, there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it may have twisting, or splitting, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not right that you move [the dislocation] with your hand, but put on medicines that come afterwards, and then hold it gently now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the break which goes into the joint, and are the two parts dislocated, you must now set them equally, so that abscesses grow not there.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if abscesses swell up, let it lie for some time until the abscess is calmed down.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then adjust it to the direction in which it can move easily and skillfully, and know that the restoration of this [dislocation] is easier than the restoration where there are bones broken; then set it as required after that.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone is broken into pieces and broken in two parts, whether it is a hand or foot, or at your hand if it is one of the small members, or at the wrist or ankle, or at the arm;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	align the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are dislocated, you reset them with every means possible and ensure that your work causes no further injury or pain to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	align well the two ends of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well with the hand if it seems to you that it is not good: straighten it carefully, and do not strain it too much, nor press as those who bring it by their work abscess hot and contraction to the limb, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is healed, punish the patient well so that he does not move it, neither in watching nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and ensure that the limb is so secure that it feels no pain at all.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	When it feels no pain, it is not broken, and it should be placed in such a position that it feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and keep that it is straightened, so twist does not come when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the qualities of the broken limb are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs can be various in smallness, size, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small members, such as arms and fingers etc.; it is necessary to wrap linen cloths soft and thin around them;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are thick, such as thighs and legs: it is necessary to wrap with a broad and hard rope, for the large ropes bind the whole large member tightly and equally from all sides, so there is no gap.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie around light bandages, three or four turns according to the member, and tighten your hand a little on the rope, then go above the break and tighten less than the break, then move away a little from the break;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And soften the ligament little by little, until you take a large part of the healthy bone, then take another ligament and turn around completely reversed over the broken bone.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then return to the part below the break, and tighten moderately, neither too strongly nor too loosely, as we said in the first lesson above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then put dampened linen or cloth strips between the ligaments until they are all even, then tie everything with one bandage, and then place your well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, place warm compresses on it and let the swelling subside for some days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then bind with strips of half a thick cane, or with cleft wood, or with palm fronds, and they should be in this manner:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but the bandage that you place over the break should be a little larger and thicker than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	And let it be as long as is required for a small or large limb.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then hold it between the stirrups in the same way you did at the first joint, then bind it with thread coming forward, as you did on the break.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	it is narrower now, yet wider; and it must be of moderate thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of flax thread.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	because if the thread is thick, as I have seen in the works of foolish people who make their bindings with twisted flax thread, and that is great error, for the binding cannot be even if it is too thin, and it should not have less than two fingers' space between each stirrup.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is gored by the heads of arrows after being stretched out in healthy places, place linen or woollen cloth over them to prevent bleeding.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is broken and the vessels ruptured, I will tell the cure after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not necessary to set arrows in all broken limbs immediately on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, it is not necessary to put arrows in them immediately, but rather after 5 or 7 days or more, according to your confidence in the abscess healing process.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And here is the manner of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsions: you should take flour that is held on the mill walls, and mix it with a lot of egg, and apply this mixture, neither too thick nor too thin, and use it; this is the common method for restoring the fracture in various positions, and especially for women and small children, for it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plaster for restoring fractures and dislocations and torsions: take barley and linseed and elder and wormwood and Arabic gum and mastic, in the quantity of ten; myrrh and aloes, in the quantity of five; elshorn flowers eight; grind them into powder and mix with a lot of egg; if the man's complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it has good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and it is useful to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another plaster for torsion: take mastic and wormwood, in the quantity of ten; myrrh and aloes, eight; acacia leaves six; Armenian balm ten; grind it well, and mix with vinegar or a lot of egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another method of plaster for joints and dislocated bones, soothes the pain arising, and heals with the bone, and breaks: take new linen, moisten it in water and cooked oil, and apply it to the place. This plaster does not restore [the limb], but it is good for soothing the pain of an abscess and a proper wound.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plaster that sets broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earth sorrel leaves, grind together, and make plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method of plaster for the restoration of broken bones and to hasten the healing of an abscess: take the root of comfrey, chamomile, violet flowers, bran, of each one part; grind together, mix with wine, and apply to the affected member when it is hot. Or, if the member is cold, use warm coriander water instead.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another method of plastering stronger than the first, when an abscess hardens in the restoration of the limb. Take root of comfrey, flax seed, balm of Gilead, clover, and wild marjoram, violet flowers and chamomile flowers, all together in equal parts; grind, and cook with salt water, sweet water, or wine according to the heat of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates states in his book that no other substance should be applied on a broken member for restoration except a plaster made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	It seems Galen suggests that dry and slightly warm substances should be applied to a broken member for restoration such as myrrh, aloes, incense and similar things as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of plaster that is good for injuries and pain: take ground up mugath (possibly a type of root) and crushed human hairs or feathers of birds, and add resin, and mix them equally, and grind them into a plaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	Then, remove the plaster a little afterward, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; do not remove it for many days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	If pain or itching comes to the place, or discomfort, without rest or swelling, hasten and remove the plaster immediately; take light cloth and sea sponge wet with seawater, and immerse the affected area until the itching stops and the pain is relieved.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the member rest for an hour, then put dry linen on it, dampen it in vinegar or rose oil, and tie it up with a nut, until you are sure of the abscess heating.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the inflammation of the member rest, and relieve the pain, then resume the binding gently, add a little plaster, and do not strain it too much as before; and bind it until it heals.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess has cooled and turned red, pain and swelling have subsided, and you need plaster and linen, resume the binding as you did before equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if no swelling comes to the limb from what has been said, do not dislocate it before 3 or 4 or 5 or 7 days; and sometimes leave it for 20 days, as one sees fit, until the break heals, and the joint approaches the flesh above;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	then hold it longer than before, and the flesh swells more as I have said before; and if you see the joint drying out too much, know that nutrients cannot enter.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	apply warm moist heat to the joint every time you dislocate it, and do this thrice a day, and slightly stretch the bandage;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Therefore, cut the nerve endings in the limb and correct immediately whatever the foolish person does, who distorts the member: it is bad, and this work is dangerous; I do not see anything else but to weaken and work correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways of breaking [bones], and various shapes, and the causes are intended.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For there are breakages that are made by sword impact, and the collar bone breaks the entire bone up to the shaft which is underneath the bone, as does a hack or cleave; and for this reason, this method of breaking is called "hackure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	For the sword strikes the bone from above causing it to pierce, and this method of breaking is called "absolute"; and these are the large or small wounds caused by these two breaks.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is piercing indentation, or cleaving or fall from stone, or falling on stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has a persistent break, which reaches up to the fabric beneath the bone or on top of the bone, and this is the wound, whether large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if it has a wound that is healed so close to the bone, as thin as hair, and this is the small fracture, which is called "capillary" fracture.
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	and if the wound is caused by hitting with stone or falling or any such thing, and it pushes the bone piece inside, and the fracture is closed tightly like a potter when he fires on top of pots; then the stone enters.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often in those who have or a moist bone head, such as a child's head;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens in all these ways of fracture where small pieces are dislocated, as in the case of a collarbone; and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all the ways of fractures by the distraction above them, and the examination with tension, and by the corrupt flesh that is on top of it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hairy bump is recognized when, when one exposes the bone and scrubs above it, the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, beware of the patient's conditions, and if you see any harmful symptoms like vomiting of blood, loss of consciousness, swelling, pain in the feet, high fever, hairs growing and reddening, and similar signs in various situations, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any harmful symptoms, and expect healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fracture first comes to you in winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the month when possible.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is a fracture, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue beneath the bone is not corrupted, and the accidents mentioned come about.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	If the fracture of the bone reaches the layer that covers the brain, then you must cut the fractured part in this manner: and it is that you grasp the head of the patient firmly, and uncover above the bone in all ways possible, and over the figure of the wound as much as you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and if the discharge of blood comes when uncovering the bone or an abscess opens up, then help with what is necessary, and it is that you fill the place with damp linen soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And make the wound rest until the abscess subsides and you are sure of stopping the flow of blood; then begin to remove the bone around it, and this is done according to two methods of treatment: one method, where you make a narrow incision in front, and this is called the "chisel" form.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then insert another incision larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have various incisions, some narrow and others wide, sharp and pointed, made of iron indeterminate; and work lightly, so as not to pierce the bone.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is dislocated and hard, you must pierce it around so as to provide relief with drills, but not to such an extent that they pass through the bone to the other side, and there should be a margin or circle on top of the point that does not allow the point to pass through the bone; and you should have more than one, each arriving at its place on the edge of the bone, so you have drills for all sides; and this is the shape of the four types of drills:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is to place one drill on the bone and turn it with your hands until you feel that the bone is pierced; then remove the drill slightly, and do this all around, then chop out the space of the bone between the fractures as delicately and lightly as possible, as we have said, until you draw out the bone to your hand or any other tool you have such as pliers or tweezers; and be careful not to touch the brain or spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	and when you have pierced the bone and treated it, it is necessary that you reset the tightness which has remained on the bone with another tool resembling a chisel, but it must be thinner and more delicate than the other chisels.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if any small bones or scales remain, gently remove them with an instrument; then treat the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of treatment is that which the Greeks say, which is more secure; and they praise it highly, and this is their word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you should cut open part of the bone where the fracture is visible, so that when you have exposed that part, place the blunt-edged leech-shaped instrument on top.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And it should not be cut from one side, and the part is sharp in two edges, so that the cut is towards the bone; then hit with a small hammer on top, so that you lightly break the bone all around, and be careful of the cloth that is underneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is attached to the bone, break it lightly, for one breaks it badly and with fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the bone does not break through to the cloth, and the bone is only broken from above, there will be small pieces; in such a case, you must smooth it out, and remove the scales with a fine rasp, having various quantities, to provide the most suitable one for each place, according to the work and the figure of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If the king shaves before with great razors, and afterward with more subtle ones, and does not stop doing so until it is well done.
